Timezone

🌍 Timezone Converter

Understanding how to convert preset timezones according to your broker's geographic location.

🚨 Critical Information: Presets ALWAYS use broker server time, NOT your local time or VPS time.

❓ Why Timezone Conversion Matters

🌐 The Timezone Challenge

ARIA V4 users presets are configured with specific trading hours that work optimally for certain market sessions. However, these hours are set according to the broker's server timezone, which varies by broker and geographic location.

📊 Example Problem:
  • Preset says: Trade from 08:00 to 17:00
  • Your expectation: European session (08:00-17:00 GMT)
  • Reality: Depends on your broker's server timezone!

🕐 Common Broker Timezones

🌍 Most Common Server Times

🇪🇺 GMT+2/GMT+3 (European Brokers)
  • Winter: GMT+2 (EET)
  • Summer: GMT+3 (EEST)
  • Examples: Many EU-regulated brokers
🇺🇸 GMT-5/GMT-4 (US Brokers)
  • Winter: GMT-5 (EST)
  • Summer: GMT-4 (EDT)
  • Examples: US-based brokers
🇦🇺 GMT+10/GMT+11 (Australian Brokers)
  • Winter: GMT+10 (AEST)
  • Summer: GMT+11 (AEDT)
  • Examples: Australian brokers
🌐 GMT+0 (London Time)
  • Winter: GMT+0 (GMT)
  • Summer: GMT+1 (BST)
  • Examples: UK-based brokers
🇧🇷 GMT-3 (South American Brokers)
  • Year-round: GMT-3 (BRT - Brazil Time)
  • Note: Some regions may observe daylight saving
  • Examples: Brazilian and some Latin American brokers

🔄 How to Convert Preset Times

📝 Step-by-Step Conversion Process

  1. 🔍 Identify Your Broker's Timezone
    • Contact broker support directly to ask for their server GMT offset
    • This is the most reliable way to get accurate timezone information
  2. 📊 Determine Preset's Original Timezone
    • Most presets are created for GMT+2/GMT+3
    • Check preset documentation if available
    • Ask directly to the person who uploaded the preset about their GMT configuration (usually users mention what GMT their broker uses so you can calculate it correctly)
  3. ⚙️ Calculate Time Difference
    • Find difference between preset timezone and your broker
    • Apply adjustment to all trading hours
    • Consider daylight saving changes

📊 Conversion Examples

🌍 Real-World Conversion Scenarios

📈 Scenario 1: European Preset → US Broker
  • Preset timezone: GMT+3 (European summer)
  • Your broker: GMT-4 (US summer)
  • Time difference: 7 hours behind
  • Preset time: 08:00-17:00
  • Your broker time: 01:00-10:00
📈 Scenario 2: European Preset → Australian Broker
  • Preset timezone: GMT+2 (European winter)
  • Your broker: GMT+10 (Australian winter)
  • Time difference: 8 hours ahead
  • Preset time: 08:00-17:00
  • Your broker time: 16:00-01:00 (next day)
📈 Scenario 3: US Preset → European Broker
  • Preset timezone: GMT-5 (US winter)
  • Your broker: GMT+2 (European winter)
  • Time difference: 7 hours ahead
  • Preset time: 09:00-18:00
  • Your broker time: 16:00-01:00 (next day)
📈 Scenario 4: European Preset → South American Broker
  • Preset timezone: GMT+2 (European winter)
  • Your broker: GMT-3 (Brazilian broker)
  • Time difference: 5 hours behind
  • Preset time: 08:00-17:00
  • Your broker time: 03:00-12:00

⚠️ Important Considerations

🚨 Critical Points to Remember

🕐 Daylight Saving Time (DST):
  • GMT offsets change twice per year
  • European DST: Last Sunday in March/October
  • US DST: Second Sunday in March, First Sunday in November
  • Update your conversions when DST changes occur
🌐 Server Time vs Local Time:
  • Always use broker server time, never your local time
  • VPS time is irrelevant for trading hours
  • Check MT5 terminal for actual server time
📅 Weekend and Holiday Considerations:
  • Market sessions may be affected by holidays
  • Some brokers have different weekend hours
  • Crypto markets operate 24/7

🔧 Practical Implementation

✅ How to Apply Timezone Conversion

  1. 📥 Download Preset
    • Get the preset file from community
    • Note the original timezone if mentioned
  2. 🔍 Check Your Broker Time
    • Contact your broker support to get their GMT offset
    • This ensures accurate timezone information
  3. ⚙️ Adjust Trading Hours
    • Apply timezone difference to all time parameters
    • Update Start Hour, End Hour for each day
    • Adjust news filter times if applicable
  4. 💾 Save Modified Preset
    • Save with new name indicating your timezone
    • Example: "EURUSD_Scalping_GMT-4.set"
  5. 🧪 Test and Verify
    • Test on demo account first
    • Verify trading hours match expected market sessions
    • Monitor for a few days to confirm timing
💡 Pro Tip: Create a personal timezone conversion chart for quick reference when downloading new presets. Keep track of your broker's GMT offset for both summer and winter periods.
📊 Final Reminder: Remember that successful trading depends not just on the right strategy, but also on trading at the right times. Proper timezone conversion ensures your EA operates during the intended market sessions for optimal performance.
Panel

New Configuration Panel

This is a completely renovated and interactive panel.

🎯 Panel Overview

From this panel, you can access all ARIA configuration without needing to edit the input parameters. This has been designed to facilitate users' configuration of ARIA, without having to look at a long list of parameters that confuse.

This panel is organized in different tabs, in a more intuitive way and with a more dynamic interface.

Panel Advantages:
  • 🎨 Intuitive Interface: No more confusing parameter lists
  • 📑 Organized Tabs: Logical grouping of settings
  • 🔄 Dynamic Interface: Interactive and user-friendly
  • ⚡ Quick Configuration: Easy navigation between settings

🔧 How the Panel Works

📋 Scenario 1: Creating New Configuration

If you don't have a specific preset, but want to start operating and choose your options within the parameters:

  1. Navigate through tabs: Simply change all the parameters you want from the panel, just navigate comfortably tab by tab and configure what you need.
  2. Save your configuration: Once configured, you can save it, give it a specific name like a normal preset, just as you would in the parameters but in a more intuitive way.
  3. Preset storage: This preset will be saved in MQL5/Files
  4. Load in ARIA: Simply open ARIA configuration, go to the Inputs tab and load that preset you configured as you normally do.
  5. Apply settings: Load / search for the preset in MQL5/Files and that's it, when you click accept, ARIA will start operating with that preset.
⚠️ Important: This last step is always necessary, because MQL5 has a restriction so that no panel can directly modify the inputs configuration tab for security reasons.

📥 Scenario 2: Using Existing Preset

If you already have a preset that was shared by another user:

  1. Load existing preset: Simply go to the Inputs tab, click Load and search for your preset and accept.
  2. Panel auto-update: Once you click accept, the panel will be updated with the data loaded from your preset.
  3. Modify if desired: From there you can modify if you want, and save the preset from the panel itself.
  4. Apply changes: Remember that for the change to be applied in the inputs tab, you must reload the modified preset in Load / load the preset and click accept.
  5. Ready to trade: Now you have a modified preset working correctly.
Workflow Summary:
  • New Configuration: Panel → Save → Load in Inputs → Accept
  • Existing Preset: Load in Inputs → Panel Updates → Modify → Save → Reload → Accept
🔄 Key Concept: The panel and inputs tab work together. The panel provides an easy interface, but changes must always be applied through the inputs tab due to MQL5 security restrictions.

📌 Panel Tabs

Within the configuration panel, we will see that there are 8 tabs:

💡 Interactive Help: All parameters that have the question mark sign (?), when clicked, open an explanatory window that details what it means and how that parameter is used.

1. 🤖 AI

  • Choice of simple query or multiple query
  • In each case: Selection of AI provider(s)
  • Maximum tokens configuration, timeout and temperature
  • Multiple query mode (Multi-AI ON/OFF)
  • Decision type (e.g. Majority Vote)
  • Activation/deactivation of each individual AI provider
  • List of available models for each provider (GPT-4, Claude, Gemini, Llama, etc.)
  • Integration with OpenRouter in Free or Paid versions

2. ✏️ PROMPT

  • Activate/deactivate Custom Prompt
  • Selection of TXT file with customized prompt
  • Multi-timeframe fractal filter (activate by timeframes: M5, M15, M30, H1, H4, D1)
  • Parameters for minimum timeframes, lookback and trend
  • Response language selection
  • AI ratio adjustments (StopLoss Ratio and TakeProfit Ratio)
  • Candle history control and number of bars to use

3. 📈 TRADING

  • Activate/deactivate Auto Mode
  • Trading mode selection (e.g. Time Mode)
  • Operation frequency configuration
  • Lot mode selection (e.g. Dynamic Risk)
  • Lot value, dynamic risk in %
  • Take Profit (TP) and Stop Loss (SL) configuration
  • Confidence level in signals
  • Additional filters by timeframe
  • Activatable news filter and impact level
  • Identifiers for automatic/manual operations (Magic Numbers)

4. 📊 INDICATORS

  • Activation/deactivation of indicators: RSI, ATR, MA200, MA50, MACD, Stochastic, Bollinger Bands, Fibonacci, S/R, Volume
  • Configuration of periods and parameters for each indicator
  • Volatility thresholds for multiple timeframes (M1 to W1)

5. ⚠️ RISK

  • Cooldown System: controls pauses between operations
  • Spread Filter: limits entry if spread is high
  • Trailing stop parameters
  • Profit/loss limits
  • TP to breakeven system
  • Support and resistance filters
  • Breakeven parameters
  • Overtrade control (Overtrade Parameters)

6. ⏰ HOURS

  • Activate/deactivate trading hours
  • Configure start and end trading by day of the week
  • Activate/deactivate weekends

7. 🧠 XGBOOST

  • Activate/deactivate integration with XGBoost model
  • API URL and data path
  • Minimum confidence parameter
  • Fallback option in case of error
  • Debug mode for testing
XGBoost Integration: Advanced machine learning model for enhanced trade analysis. Access via ARIA Audit API.

8. 🎨 CHART

  • Graphic style options
  • Show/hide grid
  • Color selection for: background, bullish/bearish candles, bars
  • Show/hide volumes and define color
Parameters

Parameters Guide

Complete parameters configuration for ARIA V4.

Single AI Consultation

Select AI Provider

This parameter is used when working with a single AI.

From the dropdown menu you choose which provider you are going to use (OpenAI, Mistral, DeepSeek, Claude, etc.).

AI Configuration

Each provider has its own section (example: Llama, Gemini, Claude, DeepSeek, Mistral, Grok).

Model to use: allows you to choose the exact model from a dropdown menu (e.g.: gpt-4-turbo, claude-3.5, mistral-large…).

OpenRouter AI #1, #2, #3, #4, #5

OpenRouter works differently because with a single API Key you can access multiple models. That's why here you have 5 spaces to configure different models at the same time.

  • Use Free Models = TRUE → uses the free model.
  • Use Free Models = FALSE → uses the paid model.
  • Free model selection: choose a free model from the dropdown.
  • Paid model selection: choose a paid model from the dropdown.
👉 This repeats 5 times: So you can have up to 5 different OpenRouter models, mixing free and paid ones.

📌 Multiple AI Consultation

Enable Multiple AI Consultation

If set to true, allows ARIA to consult multiple AIs at the same time. If set to false, the Select AI Provider parameter will be used.

Individual AI Provider Inclusion

Each provider can be activated (true) or deactivated (false):

  • Include OpenAI in multiple consultation
  • Include Llama in multiple consultation
  • Include Gemini in multiple consultation
  • Include Claude in multiple consultation
  • Include DeepSeek in multiple consultation
  • Include Mistral in multiple consultation
  • Include Grok in multiple consultation
  • Include OpenRouter AI #1 to #5 in multiple consultation

🗳️ Decision Type for Multiple AIs

Decision Type for Multiple AIs

We have 3 possible decision types:

  • Majority Decision Default = Simple majority (we recommend using this) e.g.: 3/5 AIs agree.
  • Majority Decision Custom = A majority that is customized in the parameter AI Count Required for Majority Custom Mode, example: I have 5 active AIs and I want that for a buy or sell option to be considered, 4 AIs must say sell. Not recommended for free AIs, only for advanced users.
  • Unanimous Decision = Unanimous decision, 5/5 AIs agree.
Recommendation: Use Majority Decision Default for most scenarios. It provides good balance between accuracy and trade frequency.

🧠 XGBoost ML Configuration

Enable XGBoost ML for SL/TP

When set to true, XGBoost takes control of Stop Loss and Take Profit calculations using advanced machine learning algorithms.

XGBoost API URL

Must use exclusively: https://aria-mcp-bridge.onrender.com

This is the official ARIA Audit API endpoint for XGBoost integration. Based on the [ARIA Audit API](https://aria-mcp-bridge.onrender.com), this service provides trade analysis and strategy optimization.

XGBoost Data Path

Default: xgboost\ in MT5 data directory

Local folder path for XGBoost training data files.

  • Used to store historical market data for ML training
  • Contains all files saved by XGBoost learning process
  • Location: MT5 data directory for easy access

Minimum Confidence Level

Default: 0.60 (60%)

Minimum confidence required to use XGBoost prediction.

  • Range: 0.0 (0%) to 1.0 (100%)
  • Higher values = more conservative, fewer false signals
  • Lower values = more aggressive, higher false signals

Use Fallback Mode

Default: ON

Enable fallback when XGBoost API is unavailable.

  • Uses ATR-based calculations as backup method
  • Recommended: ON for continuous trading operation
Backup Strategy: When XGBoost is unavailable, ARIA automatically switches to ATR (Average True Range) calculations to maintain trading operations without interruption.

Debug Mode

Default: OFF

Enable detailed logging for XGBoost operations.

🧠 What is XGBoost and How it Manages SL/TP Levels in ARIA

XGBoost is a statistical mathematical model, pre-trained and widely used for optimizing trading data. It was trained with 60,000 real audited trades that ARIA took live and that have been manually uploaded by users during V3, so it already starts with a knowledge base about ARIA and its trades.

🎓 Learning Process:
  • 📚 Pre-trained Base: Starts with knowledge from all V3 user audits
  • 📅 Daily Learning: Each day at the end of trading hours, XGBoost saves what it learned during the day to its memory
  • 🔍 Self-Audit: It will self-audit to see what it got wrong, what went well, and what it can improve
  • 🧠 Daily Improvement: This process is daily, so each day, it will be a little wiser
🌐 Collective Learning: Since it's a machine learning model, XGBoost learns from all trades of all ARIA users. Therefore, the more different users run ARIA, the faster it will improve.
🔍 Total Transparency:

You can always see what it learns and what it saves to memory, both in the Experts tab and in its XGBoost Folder Data Path, for complete transparency.

  • 📊 Experts Tab: Real-time learning logs and decisions
  • 📁 XGBoost Folder: Stored learning data and model updates
  • 🔍 Full Visibility: Monitor what the model learns and how it evolves

📰 News Filter

News Filter Configuration

ARIA connects to https://nfs.faireconomy.media/ to retrieve high and medium impact news related to the symbol it is currently trading.

There's no need to modify anything manually — It will automatically detect your broker's time zone.

If news is detected for the symbol, ARIA will not take any new trades, and will pause trading 30 minutes before and 30 minutes after the event.

Enable News Filter

This feature can be enabled by setting "Enable News Filter" to true, or disabled with false if you prefer ARIA to keep trading regardless of news.

News Impact Level Options

You will then have 3 options to choose from:

  • High Impact News (e.g. NFP, FOMC, Interest Rate Decisions)
  • Medium Impact News (e.g. PMI, Retail Sales, Unemployment Claims)
  • Both (High and Medium Impact)
⚠️ Keep in mind:
  • If you choose both, you may notice a reduction in the number of trades due to this filter.
  • Ideally, you should only pause trading during high impact news events.
🆕 V4 Visual Indicator: When news events are active for a currency pair and ARIA is not trading due to this filter, the chart frame will appear in red color. If the frame is green, it means the news filter allows trading on that pair because there are no active news events at that moment. If the news filter is disabled, the frame will always appear green since this means the filter "allows" new operations to be opened.
Recommended Setting: Enable filter for High Impact News only to maintain good trade frequency while avoiding major volatility events.

📐 Fractal Parameters

❓ What is it and what is it for?

It is a confirmation filter by timeframe confluence. Before allowing an operation, ARIA checks that several timeframes "agree" with the direction (bullish or bearish). The more confirmations you ask for, the fewer operations (but of higher quality) the EA will approve.

🔑 Key Idea: Confluence = quality. Without confluence or with opposite signals between timeframes, the filter denies entry.

🏆 Golden Rules (Very Important)

⚠️ Rule #1: Never include the trading timeframe within the fractal filter.
  • Example: If you trade on M5, activate M15 and higher (M15/M30/H1); do not activate M5.
  • Reason: Avoid "self-confirming" and overfitting the signal. Always confirm with higher timeframes.
  • More timeframes = fewer trades (stricter filter)
  • More minimum confirmations = more selective (discards more signals)
  • Recommended: Activate 2 confirmations from higher TFs, as more will lose many trading opportunities
  • Adjust filter to instrument and its volatility (EURUSD ≠ GOLD)

⚙️ Parameters (What they mean and how they affect)

Enable Fractal Filter

Turns on/off the multi-TF confluence system.

Timeframes to Evaluate

Select the timeframes (e.g. M15, M30, H1, H4, D1).

Remember: Only higher than the timeframe where you operate and no more than 2 TF.
Minimum Confirmations

How many of the selected TFs must agree in the same direction to allow entry.

  • 1–2 = more operations (more flexible)
  • 3–4 = fewer operations (more demanding)
Lookback Periods

How many candles back each TF looks to evaluate fractals/trend.

  • More lookback: More robust signals, but later
  • Less lookback: Faster signals, but more noise
Trend Strength (Threshold)

Minimum "consistency" (e.g., 0.6) that the filter must detect to accept.

  • Higher value: Reduces entries in sideways markets
  • Lower value: More entries, but less selective

🔧 How to Configure it (Quick Step by Step)

  1. Choose your operating timeframe (e.g.: M5, M15, H1)
  2. Activate the fractal filter
  3. Mark only higher TFs (if you operate M15 → activate M30/H1/H4)
  4. Set "Minimum Confirmations" according to your style (2 or 3)
  5. Adjust Lookback (base 10–20 candles per TF) and Strength (0.6 approx.)
  6. Test it on demo
💰 Token Consumption Warning: Remember that this parameter, when activated and sending various data from different TFs, consumes more tokens. If you are using paid models, check consumption, since if you are on very small TFs consulting every 5 minutes, consumption will skyrocket. It's different if you work from M15 onwards, where consultations are more spaced.

📚 Practical Reading

More TFs + more confirmations = more filter → fewer entries and higher probability of success in trending markets.

✅ Clear Examples (Yes/No)

🔥 I operate on M5 (scalping):
  • ✅ Yes: M15 + M30 + H1 (min. 2 conf.)
  • ❌ No: activate M5 in the filter (breaks rule #1)
📈 I operate on M30 (intraday):
  • ✅ Yes: H1 + H4 + D1 (min. 2–3 conf.)
  • ❌ No: include M30 in the list

🔗 Interactions with Other Systems

  • With spread and news: The fractal can give "OK", but if the spread is high or there is high impact news, ARIA will block anyway (filters are cumulative).
  • With schedules: Outside your trading window, operation is denied even if confluence is perfect.
  • With risk management: By requiring confluence, it reduces overtrading and stabilizes drawdown.

❌ Common Errors (and how to avoid them)

Error #1: Include the trading timeframe in the filter ⇒ No (rule #1). You will block almost everything or self-confirm.
Error #2: Activate too many TFs with many confirmations (e.g. 5 TF and ask for 4) ⇒ you run out of operations. Start with 2–3 TF with 2 conf. and increase if necessary.
Error #3: Use the same preset for all symbols ⇒ GOLD/indices require more relaxed configurations (high volatility).
Error #4: Very short lookback ⇒ "fragile" signals and more noise; too long ⇒ you arrive late. Start at 10–20.

⏸️ Cooldown

❓ What is it and what does it solve?

The Cooldown is an automatic pause between operations to avoid over-trading right after an SL or TP. During that window, ARIA does not open new positions (according to your configuration), which helps to cut streaks, reduce "revenge trading" and let the market stabilize before the next trade.

🎯 Main Benefits:
  • 🛑 Prevents over-trading after SL/TP events
  • 😤 Reduces revenge trading impulses
  • 📊 Market stabilization time
  • 📉 Cuts losing streaks

⚙️ Where it's configured and what parameters it has

In the Filters/Systems panel you will see the Cooldown controls:

  • Enable Cooldown: activates/deactivates the system
  • Cooldown Minutes: duration of the pause (e.g., 1–180 min)
  • Apply on SL: if cooldown is triggered when closing by Stop Loss
  • Apply on TP: if cooldown is triggered when closing by Take Profit
  • Per Symbol (per-symbol): cooldown affects only the instrument of that closure; if deactivated, cooldown can be global
📌 Note: Filters in ARIA are cumulative. Even if Cooldown "lets a trade pass", other filters (spread, news, schedules, fractal, etc.) can block it and vice versa.

🔄 How it Works (Real Flow)

  1. Position closes by SL and/or TP (according to what you marked)
  2. ARIA registers the event and starts the cooldown countdown
  3. While cooldown is active, no new operations are launched from the chosen scope (symbol or global)
  4. Time completed, the system becomes available again without you having to do anything
Example Flow:

EURUSD trade closes with SL → 30-minute cooldown starts → No new EURUSD trades → Timer expires → Normal trading resumes

✅ Practical Benefits

  • 🎯 Controls impulse to re-enter immediately after an SL or large TP
  • 🌊 Avoids "accelerated" markets after a breakout or news, when spread/volatility has not yet normalized
  • 📊 Stabilizes drawdown and lowers variance by spacing decisions

🔗 Important Interactions

With Other Filters
  • Spread / News / Schedules: If any of these filters is blocking, cooldown doesn't "force" anything; the trade still doesn't pass. Think of cooldown as another layer of temporal security.
With Overtrading Control
  • Complementary systems: Cooldown cuts by time; anti-overtrading cuts by time and/or price distance
  • Double lock: Use them together when the market is "nervous"
With Profit/Loss Limits
  • Priority system: If you reach a daily limit and the EA is paused, the limit pause takes priority; cooldown is secondary
Multi-Symbol Trading
  • Per Symbol active: You can have EURUSD in cooldown and continue operating GBPUSD
  • Global: Everything stops

❌ Common Errors (and how to avoid them)

Error #1: Minutes too low → doesn't avoid market over-reaction. Increase gradually and test on demo.
Error #2: Only TP or only SL when your strategy needs both. If you see streaks after any closure, enable both triggers.
Error #3: Global unintentionally: if you operate multiple symbols, activate per symbol to not freeze the entire setup.
Error #4: "Never operates": sometimes it's not the cooldown but other filters (spread, news, schedules). Check the status panel to see which filter blocked the trade.

🎯 TP to Breakeven

❓ What is TP to Breakeven?

It is a hybrid function between take profit and breakeven.

The logic is: when the price reaches a certain partial TP level, the EA automatically moves the SL to the entry price (or with a small positive margin).

📊 Practical Example:
  1. You open a buy on EURUSD at 1.1000
  2. You configure TP-to-BE at +30 pips
  3. When price reaches 1.1030, the EA moves your SL from 1.1000 → 1.1005 (5 pips secured profit)
  4. This way you lock partial profit and prevent the operation from going negative

⚙️ Configuration Parameters

In ARIA it appears as "TP → BE" system and depends on parameters like:

  • Activation Distance (pips): How many pips profit needed to trigger
  • Offset (additional pips): Extra pips above entry price for safety
  • Activation Conditions: Always after a mini-TP is reached
🎯 Use Case: Perfect for scalping and intraday strategies where you want to secure partial profits quickly.

🔒 Breakeven

❓ What is Breakeven?

Simpler system: when the trade advances in favor X pips, the EA moves the SL to exact entry price (or entry + offset).

Ensures that the operation does not close at a loss, but without needing to reach the TP.

📊 Example:
  1. Buy at 1.1000
  2. Breakeven activated at +20 pips
  3. When price touches 1.1020, SL moves to 1.1000
  4. Result: Either you win or exit without loss

⚠️ Important Compatibility Note

⚠️ Warning: In ARIA it is not recommended to use Breakeven and Trailing at the same time, because both try to move the SL and enter into conflict.

📈 Trailing Options

1. Trailing OFF

  • The system is deactivated
  • ARIA will not move the Stop Loss automatically
  • Only managed with fixed SL, fixed TP, TP→BE or AI management, according to what you have active

2. Trailing in Pips

It is the classic trailing, based on distance in pips.

Main Parameters:
  • Start: how many pips profit the trade must advance for it to activate
  • Step: every how many pips the SL will be updated
  • Distance: the constant separation it will maintain with respect to the current price
📌 Example:
  • Buy EURUSD at 1.1000
  • Trailing Start = 20 pips, Distance = 15
  • When it reaches 1.1020 → activates and SL rises to 1.1005
  • At 1.1030 → SL rises to 1.1015
  • And so on...
✅ Useful for: Stable pairs with "clean" movements (EURUSD, GBPUSD).

3. Trailing in Percent (RECOMMENDED)

Instead of pips, it is based on a percentage of floating profit.

1. Trailing Start (0.05)

Defines from what percentage of floating profit the trailing is activated.

  • Example: 0.05 = 5%
  • When the operation reaches +5% profit relative to risk/position, dynamic trailing is activated
2. Trailing Stop (0.025)

Indicates the minimum percentage of profit that is secured once trailing is active.

  • Example: 0.025 = 2.5%
  • Even if the market retraces, the EA will move the Stop Loss to always have at least +2.5% of the operation secured
3. Trailing Step (0.01)

Defines how often the trailing is adjusted, expressed as additional percentage.

  • Example: 0.01 = 1%
  • For every +1% extra that the price advances, the SL will be readjusted to maintain the security proportion
📊 Practical Example with these values:

Suppose an operation opens and profit begins to grow:

  • +3% profit → Nothing happens, trailing not yet active
  • +5% profit → Trailing activates. SL moves to guarantee +2.5%
  • +6% profit → SL adjusts again (1% Step). Now secures +3.5% approx.
  • +7% profit → SL rises again. Secures +4.5%, and so on

🔄 Key Difference vs. Trailing Pips

Comparison:
  • In pips: Everything is fixed: distance in price points
  • In percent: Everything is dynamic: depends on how much the operation is winning

This makes Trailing Percent ideal for very volatile assets (GOLD, BTC, indices), because it automatically adapts to the movement.

📊 System Comparison Table

System When it activates How it protects Typical use
TP → BE When touching a mini-TP Secures partial profit and eliminates risk Scalping or intraday strategies
Breakeven When advancing X pips in favor Eliminates risk (no loss, no extra profit secured) Conservative strategies
Trailing When exceeding a pip threshold Locks more and more profit following the price Swing or strong trends

⚠️ Compatibility

✅ Compatible:
  • TP → BE + Trailing: Can be used together, because TP-BE secures the first protection and then Trailing follows the price
❌ Not Compatible:
  • Breakeven + Trailing: NOT compatible, generate technical conflicts

📊 Support/Resistance Filter

❓ What is it for?

The Support/Resistance (S/R) filter avoids entering just against a relevant technical level (ceiling/floor). If the price is too close to a resistance (for buys) or to a support (for sells), it blocks the operation. It can also let breakouts pass when the separation exceeds your tolerance.

🎯 Key Logic:
  • 🛑 Blocks entries against strong S/R levels
  • 🚀 Allows breakouts when price moves beyond tolerance
  • 📊 Technical protection against bad entries

🔍 How ARIA Determines S/R (User View)

  1. Looks at candle history (lookback) and detects candidate levels
  2. Only considers confirmed levels with a minimum of "touches" (retest)
  3. Uses ATR-based tolerance to count those touches as valid (doesn't require exact price to the pip)
  4. Evaluates if your entry would be too close to the level: if yes, blocks; if not, allows (or interprets as possible breakout)
🔑 Key Idea: More touches = stronger level. Lower tolerance = stricter filter.

⚙️ Parameters in the Panel

Enable S/R Filter

Activates/deactivates the filter.

Lookback Periods

How many candles it uses to search for levels (e.g., 50).

  • More lookback: Finds "historical" stronger levels (but fewer signals)
  • Less lookback: More recent levels, more signals
Min Touches

How many times the level must have been "touched" to consider it valid (e.g., 3).

  • More touches: More reliable level → more selective filter
  • Fewer touches: More levels detected, less selective
Touch Tolerance (% ATR)

Margin to consider that a touch was "at the same level".

  • High tolerance: Encompasses more touches (more valid levels, stricter filter)
  • Low tolerance: Requires more precise touches
Use High/Low vs Use Close
  • Use High/Low: Validates levels with candle highs/lows (more purist)
  • Use Close: Validates levels with closes (more conservative with long wicks)
📌 Base Recommendation: Use High/Low = ON to detect "real" ceilings/floors; activate Use Close only if your instrument has very noisy wicks (indices, crypto).

🧠 How the Filter "Thinks" When Deciding

  • Buy: If entry price falls within tolerance of a confirmed resistance, blocks (you're buying "below the ceiling")
  • Sell: If price is within tolerance of a support, blocks (you'd be selling "above the floor")
  • Breakouts: If your price is beyond level + tolerance (buy above broken resistance / sell below broken support), lets pass and considers valid breakout

🔗 Important Interactions

With Automatic Modes (Time / Breakout / Trend-Follow)

In Breakout/Trend-Follow, S/R is gold: confirms you're breaking (or respecting) levels, avoiding entries against the level.

With Other Filters

All filters are cumulative: even if S/R "lets pass", high Spread or News can still block.

With Trailing/Breakeven/TP→BE

S/R only decides entry. Management (trailing, BE, TP→BE) operates after and doesn't interfere with S/R.

⚠️ Overfiltering: If you combine Fractal + S/R + Hours + News with strict parameters, it's normal for frequency to drop a lot; adjust one at a time.

❌ Common Errors (and how to avoid them)

Error #1: Very short lookback → detects weak/random levels. Increase to 50–60 candles (majors) or 60–80 (volatiles).
Error #2: Min Touches too high → almost no valid levels → too many entries (because it "doesn't see" the level) or none (if tolerance is also large).
Error #3: Very low tolerance on volatile instruments → system "doesn't see" legitimate touches and underestimates levels.
Error #4: Using Close = OFF on assets with long wicks → filter becomes too "nervous"; consider Close = ON.
Error #5: Not checking symbol's ATR → tolerance in % ATR loses meaning if ATR doesn't adjust to the timeframe you use.

📏 Spread Filter

🎯 Spread Filter Objective

This filter is one of the most practical protections the system has, because it directly controls the cost of entering the market.

The spread is the difference between Bid and Ask price. When it widens too much (brokers in low liquidity, dead hours or strong news), entering at that moment is almost always disadvantageous.

The Spread Filter:
  • 🚫 Blocks trade opening if spread exceeds the limit you configure
  • 📊 Optionally uses spread average to avoid false blocks by momentary spikes

⚙️ Spread Filter Parameters

Enable Spread Filter

Activates or deactivates the filter.

Max Spread (in pips)

Maximum allowed value. Example: 3.0 pips on EURUSD.

If current spread is greater → EA does not open operation.

Use Average

If activated, doesn't take a single tick, but the average spread over a period.

This avoids blocks by half-second micro-spikes.

Average Periods

Number of candles/periods used to calculate that average.

Typical example: 10 periods.

🧠 How it Works in Practice

  1. EA measures spread in real time
  2. If value exceeds your allowed maximum, entry signal is discarded even if AIs give "Buy/Sell"
  3. If you have average activated, compares against average of last X periods
  4. If spread returns to normal → system allows entries again

✅ Benefits

  • 🛡️ Protection against brokers in low liquidity hours
  • 📰 Avoids operations in news with 5x or 10x larger spread
  • 📊 Improves result consistency, because you don't pay exaggerated entry costs
  • 🤝 Complements very well News Filter and Trading Hours

❌ Common Errors

Error #1: Configure maximum spread too low:
  • Example: 1.0 pip on GOLD (where normal is 8–15)
  • Result: EA almost never enters
Error #2: Configure too high:
  • Example: 10 pips on EURUSD
  • Result: Enters at times when cost is prohibitive
Error #3: Not activating average on pairs with frequent micro-spikes → false blocks.

🤖 AutoTrading

AutomodeEnabled = true / false

This parameter defines whether ARIA operates automatically or only manually:

✅ AutomodeEnabled = true

  • EA analyzes, consults AIs and opens operations by itself when conditions are met
  • Complete automated flow: AI + filters + risk management works without intervention
  • Normal mode for automatic trading

❌ AutomodeEnabled = false

  • EA does not open new operations by itself
  • But it does manage those you open manually (from Panel or from MT5):
  • Dynamic SL/TP
  • Breakeven / Trailing / TP→BE
  • AI closures (if you allow it)
  • Ideal when you want to use ARIA as advanced manager and not as 100% automatic system

⚙️ Trading Mode

Trading Mode (3 available options)

ARIA has three entry logic modes, which define how it interprets signals and filters opportunities:

🕒 a) Time Mode

Operates at fixed time intervals, according to the frequency you configure (e.g. every 15 min, every 1 hour).

At each interval, ARIA makes a query to the AIs and decides whether to open or not.

  • ✅ Advantage: Total control over operation frequency and AI costs
  • ❌ Disadvantage: May give entries even if there's no strong technical event (just by "time turn")
  • 👉 Used a lot in: Scalping and intraday

💥 b) Breakout Mode

Designed to operate key level breakouts (support/resistance, consolidations).

EA waits for price to exit a range and consults AIs if the breakout has real strength.

  • ✅ Advantage: Captures explosive movements (news, range breaks)
  • ❌ Disadvantage: Fewer operations, more sensitive to false breakouts if you don't calibrate tolerance and filters well
  • 👉 Very useful in: Volatile pairs, GOLD, BTC, indices

📈 c) Trend Follow Mode

Only seeks to enter in favor of the main trend.

Uses direction filters (MAs, fractal, AI) to ensure not going against the major flow.

  • ✅ Advantage: High probability operations in trending contexts
  • ❌ Disadvantage: In sideways ranges can give very few signals or enter late
  • 👉 Ideal for: Swing trading and letting long trends run

⚠️ Important Notes

Single Mode Only: You can only have 1 trading mode active at a time.

The Spread Filter, News, S/R, Fractal, Cooldown, etc. apply equally in any of the three modes (filters are cumulative).

🔄 Combination Examples:
  • AutomodeEnabled = false + Trading Mode = Trend Follow → only manages manual trades that go in favor of the trend
  • AutomodeEnabled = true + Trading Mode = Breakout → 100% automatic system, focused only on breakouts

⏱️ Frequency Parameters

❓ What do they control?

They control how often ARIA consults the AI to analyze the market and decide whether to open an operation.

They are normally expressed in minutes.

📊 Examples:
  • Frequency = 15 min → EA asks the AI every 15 minutes
  • Frequency = 60 min → Once per hour

⚖️ Frequency Impact

⚠️ Lower Frequency (More Often)

  • 📈 More potential operations
  • 💸 More API consumption (cost)

⚠️ Higher Frequency (Less Often)

  • 📉 Fewer operations
  • 💰 Less AI cost
👉 Recommendation: Calibrate based on trading style (scalping = lower, swing = higher).

🎯 Confidence to Trade

❓ What is it?

It is the minimum confidence level (%) that ARIA requires in the AI response to execute an operation.

📊 Example:
  • Confidence = 70% → if AI returns Buy with 65% confidence, EA does NOT open
  • If it returns Buy with 82%, EA does open

⚖️ Confidence Impact

  • Higher values = fewer operations but more quality
  • Lower values = more operations but more noise and risk
👉 Typical Range: 60–75%
  • Scalping: Better higher (70–75%)
  • Swing: You can try something lower (60–65%) to not lose long-term opportunities

💰 Lot Management Parameters

❓ What does it define?

Here you define how the EA calculates the lot size of each operation. You have 3 modes:

a) Dynamic (Risk Based) ⭐ RECOMMENDED

The lot is calculated according to a risk % on your balance/equity and the SL distance.

📊 Example (as in your image):
  • Dynamic Risk Percentage = 2.0
  • This means each operation will risk 2% of your account up to the Stop Loss
  • If your balance is $1,000, and SL = 100 pips → lot will be necessary so that, if it hits SL, you lose $20 (2%)
✅ It's the most professional method, automatically adapts lot to risk.

b) Fixed

You use a fixed lot always.

Example: Lot Value = 1.0 → always opens with 1.0 lot regardless of balance or SL.
  • ✅ Useful for: Simple backtests
  • ❌ Dangerous on small accounts, because it doesn't scale risk

c) Percentage (Lot Scaling)

The lot is calculated as a % of total balance, not based on SL.

📊 Example:
  • Lot Value = 2 → means it opens a lot equivalent to 2% of balance
  • Balance $1,000 → lot = 0.02
  • Balance $10,000 → lot = 0.20
  • ✅ Scales with balance
  • ❌ Doesn't consider SL distance → real risk can vary

⚙️ Where to place each value according to the Lot you use

Configuration Example:
  • Lot Value = 1.0 (this value is ignored in Dynamic; would only be used in Fixed or Percentage)
  • Dynamic Risk Percentage = 2.0 → Each operation will risk 2% of your account up to the Stop Loss

Example: balance $5,000 → maximum risk $100 per trade.

🎯 SL/TP Parameters

❓ What do they configure?

Here you configure how Stop Loss (SL) and Take Profit (TP) levels are calculated and placed.

Both SL and TP have their own calculation mode and an associated value.

⚙️ SL Mode and TP Mode Options

📊 Percentage

SL or TP calculated as a % of price or balance.

Example: SL = 1% → if balance is $10,000, maximum risk will be $100.

It's a mode proportional to account size.

📏 Fixed Pips

Fixed SL or TP in pips.

Example: SL = 30 → always places a Stop at 30 pips distance from entry.

It's a rigid system (doesn't adapt to volatility).

🤖 AI Recommendation

SL/TP levels are suggested by AI after analyzing market situation.

Example: AI can suggest SL at a relevant support and TP at the next resistance.

Very dynamic, but depends on AI connection stability.

📊 Swing ATR

Calculates SL/TP based on ATR (Average True Range) of the timeframe.

Example: ATR = 50 pips on H1; if you configure multiplier = 2, SL = 100 pips.

Adapts to current asset volatility.

🧠 XGBoost Machine Learning (Advanced Mode from V4)
⚠️ Important: Must have activated in the parameter Enable XGBoost ML for SL/TP = True to allow connection.

The XGBoost model evaluates volatility, market structure and historical results to dynamically optimize SL and TP.

🎓 Learning Process:
  • 📚 Learns with each operation: adjusts levels better after hits/misses
  • 🧠 Most "intelligent" option: evolutionary system
  • 📈 Daily improvement: refines decisions each day

⚙️ Associated Parameters

SL Parameter Value (in PIPS)
  • If mode is Fixed Pips: here you define exact pips (e.g. 30)
  • If mode is ATR: here you define the multiplier (e.g. 2 × ATR)
  • If it's Percentage: here you define the % (e.g. 1%)
  • In AI or XGBoost mode: this value is not taken into account
TP Parameter Value (in PIPS)

Same logic as SL: defines distance or multiplier according to chosen mode.

Example: TP Mode = Fixed Pips, TP Value = 60 → always places a Take Profit at 60 pips.

🚀 XGBoost Mode Summary

When you are with SL and TP in XGBoost mode, you are in a 100% dynamic mode, where ARIA adjusts SL and TP according to XGBoost learning and current market conditions.

🎓 Continuous Improvement: Keep in mind that each day it will improve and refine its decisions.
🧠 XGBoost Advantages:
  • 📊 Market Structure Analysis: Considers current volatility and patterns
  • 📚 Historical Learning: Based on 58,000 real audited trades
  • 🔄 Daily Evolution: Self-improves with each trading session
  • 🎯 Optimized Levels: Dynamic SL/TP based on ML predictions

⚖️ AI Risk-Reward Ratio

❓ What is AI RISK-REWARD RATIO?

The AI RISK-REWARD RATIO CONFIGURATION parameter in ARIA Connector EA refers to the system that allows defining the risk-reward relationship (SL/TP) that the AI must respect when suggesting or executing operations.

🔎 How it works

  1. User establishes a fixed ratio between Stop Loss (SL) and Take Profit (TP)
  2. Example: 1:2 means that if SL is at 50 pips, TP will automatically be at 100 pips
  3. When this system is activated, AI doesn't suggest arbitrary values, but must always adjust to that preconfigured proportion
  4. AI analyzes market conditions and adapts levels to that framework, verifying they are coherent with supports, resistances and volatility

⚙️ Main Parameters

  • SL Ratio: Risk part. (E.g.: 1 in a 1:2 ratio)
  • TP Ratio: Reward part. (E.g.: 2 in a 1:2 ratio)
  • Use Ratio System: Activates or deactivates this logic
📊 Ratio Examples:
  • 1:1 → Conservative (equal risk and reward)
  • 1:2 → Balanced (risk 50 pips, reward 100 pips)
  • 1:3 → Aggressive (risk 30 pips, reward 90 pips)

🧠 AI Flexibility

⚠️ Important: This parameter will be respected if the AIs find that ratio viable. If they don't see that ratio as possible but do see a good trade opportunity, they will recommend a different ratio.
🎯 Smart Adaptation: AI prioritizes good trading opportunities over rigid ratios, ensuring you don't miss profitable trades due to inflexible risk-reward requirements.

🚫 Overtrade Control

❓ What is overtrading?

Opening too many operations in a short time or too close to each other. This multiplies risk, generates negative correlation (all operations can lose together) and triggers unnecessary commissions/spreads.

The OVERTRADE CONTROL PARAMETERS block in ARIA Connector EA is designed to avoid overtrading, one of the most common errors that leads to excessive losses.

⚙️ Main System Parameters

Check Existing Positions

Prevents the EA from opening multiple operations on the same symbol simultaneously.

With this, each pair/asset will only have one active position at a time.

Minimum Time Between Trades (seconds)

Defines how much time must pass between closing a trade and opening the next one.

Example: 60 seconds → EA waits at least 1 minute before operating that instrument again.
Minimum Distance in Pips

Prevents opening a new operation too close to the previous one in terms of price.

Example: 50 pips → if there's already a trade on EURUSD at 1.1000, the next one won't open until price is at least at 1.1050 or 1.0950.

✅ Benefits of Overtrading Control

  • 🛡️ Reduces overexposure risk
  • 🎯 Avoids "clusters" of entries at the same price level
  • 😤 Protects against emotional trading (like trying to quickly recover a loss)
  • 📈 Increases average trade quality, because it forces waiting for better setups

⚠️ Important Warnings

Too Strict Settings:
  • Example: 1 trade per hour and 100 pips separation
  • Result: EA almost never operates
Too Lax Settings:
  • Example: 5 seconds and 5 pips
  • Result: Filter has no real effect
📊 Instrument-Specific Adjustment: It's recommended to adjust according to instrument: quiet pairs like EURUSD require fewer filters than very volatile assets like GOLD or GBPJPY.

🔧 Configuration Guidelines

📊 Recommended Settings by Asset:
  • EURUSD/GBPUSD: 30-60 seconds, 20-30 pips
  • GOLD/XAUUSD: 60-120 seconds, 50-100 pips
  • Crypto/Indices: 120-300 seconds, 100-200 pips

🔄 Mid-Trade AI Query Enable

❓ What is Mid-Trade AI Query?

Function: If set to true, AI will continue making queries even with operations already open.

Objective: Allow AI to recommend moving SL/TP, partial close, or early exit from a trade.

🎯 Configuration Recommendations

🔒 FALSE (Default) - Recommended
  • 🛡️ Safer and simpler
  • ⚠️ Conflict prevention: This parameter generates conflicts with several other ARIA filters
  • 👥 Target users: Automated traders who prefer set-and-forget approach
  • ✅ Best for: Users who want to avoid parameter conflicts
🔓 TRUE - Advanced Users Only
  • 🎯 Dynamic management: AI can adjust trades in real-time
  • ⚠️ Incompatible with: Breakeven and Trailing Stop
  • 👥 Target users: Manual traders who want AI assistance during trades
  • 🔧 Requirements: Must disable Breakeven and Trailing systems

⚠️ Important Conflicts

🚫 Cannot be used together:
  • Mid-Trade AI Query = TRUE
  • + Breakeven System
  • + Trailing Stop System

Reason: These systems compete for trade management control, causing unpredictable behavior.

🔒 Hidden SL/TP Enable

❓ What is Hidden SL/TP?

Function: Hides Stop Loss (SL) and Take Profit (TP) levels from the broker.

Objective: Prevent some brokers from doing "stop hunting" (hunting your levels).

How it works: EA saves levels internally and closes the operation when price touches them.

⚠️ Important Warnings

🔌 Connection Risk:
  • If MT5 disconnects, broker won't see those levels
  • Safety SL and TP will still be active as backup
  • But main hidden levels become inactive during disconnection
👨‍💻 Advanced Users Only:
  • Requires understanding of MT5 disconnection risks
  • Only activate if you suspect broker manipulation
  • Not recommended for beginners

🚫 System Conflicts

🔒 Hidden SL/TP Limitations:
❌ Hidden SL/TP + Mid-Trade AI Query
  • Problem: Mid-Trade queries AI about "visible" SL/TP
  • Issue: If hidden, desynchronization risk
  • Result: AI analyzes different levels than EA manages
❌ Hidden SL/TP + Trailing Stop
  • Problem: Trailing wants to move SL on server
  • Issue: If hidden, EA manages internally
  • Result: Misalignments, unexpected closes, or execution failures
❌ Hidden SL/TP + Breakeven
  • Problem: Breakeven wants to move SL to entry point
  • Issue: If hidden, EA must do it virtually
  • Result: Control duplication and possible errors

✅ Best Practice Conclusion

🎯 Recommended Usage:
  • Use Hidden SL/TP only if you want to hide levels from broker
  • Keep disabled: Mid-Trade, Trailing, and Breakeven
  • Alternative: If you want dynamic management (Trailing/Breakeven), set Hidden = false

📈 Additional Timeframe Analysis

🔍 Additional Timeframe Enable

Function: Allows AI to use an additional timeframe besides the main one where EA runs.

Objective: Analyze confluence of timeframes (example: you operate on M15, but also validate on H1).

📊 Example: EA runs on M5, but also checks H1 for trend confirmation before entering trades.

⚙️ Select Additional Timeframe

Function: Defines which extra timeframe will be used if you activate the previous point.

📈 Example: H1 → Even if your EA is on another timeframe (e.g., M5 or M15), it will also consider trends and patterns on H1 before confirming an entry.
⚠️ Important Rule: Never use the same timeframe as trading, must be superior (e.g., if you operate on M5, you can add M15 or H1, but not M5 again).

✅ Advantages vs ⚠️ Disadvantages

✅ Advantages
  • 📊 Higher precision: Multi-timeframe confluence
  • 🛡️ Fewer false signals: Better filtering
  • 📈 Trend confirmation: Superior timeframe validation
⚠️ Disadvantages
  • 📉 Fewer operations: System becomes more selective
  • ⏱️ Slower entries: More validation required
  • 🎯 Higher selectivity: May miss some opportunities

🆚 Additional TF vs Fractal Confirmation

Characteristic Additional TF Fractal Confirmation
Number of timeframes 1 additional 2 to 6 additional
Type of analysis General (AI reviews both frames) Specific (fractals + trend strength)
Flexibility Simple (basic confluence) Very configurable (min confirmations, strength, lookback)
Impact on trade frequency Moderate (slightly reduces frequency) High (can greatly reduce entries)
📝 Summary:
  • Additional Timeframe Enable = Add one extra frame for quick validation
  • Fractal Confirmation = Advanced multi-timeframe system with stricter and customizable rules

📊 Candle History Parameters

📈 Include Candle History in Prompts

Function: When set to true, EA adds candle history (OHLC data: Open, High, Low, Close, Volume) in each query sent to AI.

Objective: Give AI context about recent market behavior so it doesn't only see current price, but also previous trend, supports, resistances, and volatility.

🔎 How AI Uses This Data

✅ When TRUE:
  • 📊 Rich context: AI receives block with recent candles (example: last 200 candles)
  • 🎯 Pattern detection: Can detect double tops, breakouts, indecision candles, tested supports, etc.
  • 📈 Historical analysis: Understands market structure and price action
❌ When FALSE:
  • 📸 Snapshot only: AI only analyzes current market photo without past data
  • ⚡ Faster decisions: But less fundamentally sound
  • 🎯 Limited context: No historical pattern recognition

✅ Advantages of Activation (TRUE)

  • 🧠 AI understands historical context
  • 📊 Improved technical pattern detection
  • 🎯 Better precision in SL/TP levels and entry points
  • 📈 Enhanced trend analysis
  • 🔍 Support/resistance identification

⚠️ Disadvantages

  • 💰 Higher cost: Each query includes more data → more tokens with paid AI
  • ⏱️ Slower responses: AI responses may take a few seconds longer
  • 📉 Overkill for scalping: Not necessary for very short scalping (e.g., M1-M5), because recent candle patterns weigh more than long history

🎯 Usage Recommendations

📊 Recommended by Trading Style:
  • Scalping (M1-M5): FALSE → Speed over context
  • Day Trading (M15-H1): TRUE → Balance of context and speed
  • Swing Trading (H4-D1): TRUE → Historical context crucial
💡 Summary:
  • TRUE = More context, more precision, more cost
  • FALSE = Less context, more speed and economy

🟢 Bullish Engulfing H4 Enable

❓ What is Bullish Engulfing H4?

This parameter activates an additional filter based on a Japanese candlestick pattern: Bullish Engulfing detected on H4 timeframe.

📊 Bullish Engulfing Pattern: A bullish candle that completely engulfs the previous bearish candle, indicating potential upward reversal.

🔎 How It Works

  1. 📈 H4 Analysis: EA analyzes 4-hour (H4) candles
  2. 🎯 Pattern Detection: When it detects a Bullish Engulfing pattern
  3. 📈 BUY Only: Will only allow BUY entries
  4. ✅ Extra Confirmation: Serves as additional confirmation of bullish strength in market

✅ Advantages

  • 🎯 Filters BUY entries in zones of possible bullish reversal
  • 📊 Reinforces success probability by confirming classic reversal pattern
  • 📈 Multi-timeframe validation: Useful for swing trading or when operating on lower timeframes (M15, H1) but wanting H4 validation
  • 🔍 Classic pattern recognition: Based on proven Japanese candlestick analysis

⚠️ Limitations

🚫 BUY Only Filter:
  • Only affects BUY operations, not SELL operations
  • No sense activating if you only trade sells or neutral strategies
📉 Reduced Frequency:
  • Reduces number of trades, as pattern doesn't appear frequently
  • May miss bullish movements that don't have this prior pattern
⏱️ H4 Dependency:
  • Depends on H4 candle formation
  • May delay entries waiting for pattern confirmation

🎯 Configuration Summary

✅ Bullish Engulfing H4 Enable = TRUE

Result: Only opens BUY trades if it detects bullish engulfing pattern on H4

Best for: Conservative BUY-focused strategies with pattern confirmation

❌ Bullish Engulfing H4 Enable = FALSE

Result: EA ignores this filter and doesn't require pattern confirmation

Best for: More frequent trading without pattern restrictions

📊 Usage Recommendations

🎯 Activate when:
  • You focus primarily on BUY trades
  • You want additional reversal confirmation
  • You prefer quality over quantity in entries
  • You're swing trading or position trading
🚫 Don't activate when:
  • You trade both directions equally
  • You focus on SELL trades
  • You want maximum trade frequency
  • You're scalping on very low timeframes

💰 Profit/Loss Limits

❓ What does this parameter control?

It's a global profit or loss limit.

Unlike the SL/TP per trade calculated by ARIA XGBoost, this parameter applies to the entire trading session (day, week, or active cycle).

📊 Key Difference:
  • Individual SL/TP: Calculated by ARIA XGBoost per trade
  • Global Limits: Apply to accumulated results across all trades in session

🎯 How It Works

📈 Profit Limit

Function: If you reach certain level of accumulated gains → EA stops opening new operations.

Purpose: Protect profits and avoid giving back gains in overtrading.

📉 Loss Limit

Function: If you reach certain level of accumulated losses → EA cuts the session to protect capital.

Purpose: Damage control and capital preservation.

⚙️ Step-by-Step Configuration

💚 Profit Limit Setup
  1. Enable Profit Limit = true
    • Activates global profit control
    • Example: if you set 1000, when EA earns $1000 (accumulated across multiple operations), it stops opening more trades
  2. Profit Limit Type = Fixed Amount in Money
    • Indicates limit is in money (not percentage or pips)
    • Generally used in USD or account base currency
  3. Profit Limit Amount = X
    • Here you define the profit threshold
    • Example: 1000.0 → session closes with $1000 profit
🔴 Loss Limit Setup
  1. Enable Loss Limit = true
    • Activates global loss control
    • Very important to protect yourself from bad days
  2. Loss Limit Type = Fixed Amount in Money
    • Same as profit: limit expressed in money
    • Absolute value (positive number representing loss)
  3. Loss Limit Amount = X
    • Here you define maximum you're willing to lose in a day or session
    • Example: 500.0 → if you lose $500, EA stops automatically

🎯 Real Usage Example

📊 Configuration Example:
  • Profit Limit: $1000
  • Loss Limit: $500
  • Starting Balance: $10,000
📈 Scenario A: Profit Limit Reached
  • Result: You earn $1020 total
  • Action: EA stops opening trades
  • Benefit: Protects accumulated gains
  • Status: Successful session preserved
📉 Scenario B: Loss Limit Reached
  • Result: You lose $520 total
  • Action: EA stops immediately
  • Benefit: Prevents further losses
  • Status: Damage controlled

💡 Best Practices

🎯 Recommended Ratios:
  • Conservative: Profit Limit 2:1 Loss Limit (e.g., $1000 profit, $500 loss)
  • Balanced: Profit Limit 1.5:1 Loss Limit (e.g., $750 profit, $500 loss)
  • Aggressive: Profit Limit 1:1 Loss Limit (e.g., $500 profit, $500 loss)
⚠️ Important Considerations:
  • Account Size: Limits should be proportional to account balance
  • Risk Tolerance: Never risk more than you can afford to lose
  • Session Reset: Limits typically reset daily or per trading session
  • Existing Trades: EA may close existing trades when limits are reached

⏰ Trading Hours Control

❓ What do trading hours control?

Trading hours parameters allow you to restrict when the EA can open new positions, providing precise control over your trading schedule and market exposure.

🎯 Main Functions

🔒 Operation Opening Restriction
  • Active hours: EA only opens trades within defined time range
  • Outside hours: No new entries (but can close existing trades)
  • Flexibility: Existing positions can be managed regardless of time
📅 Weekly Management
  • Day selection: Activate or deactivate trading by day of week
  • Examples: Avoid Sundays or Friday afternoons
  • Custom schedules: Different hours for different days
🌐 Broker Server Synchronization
  • ⚠️ Very important: Hours are NOT your local time nor your VPS time
  • Server time: Uses your MT5 broker server time!!
  • Timezone awareness: Must account for broker's timezone

⚙️ Typical Parameters Configuration

🔧 Basic Settings
Enable Trading Hours Control

Options: TRUE/FALSE

Function: Activate or deactivate time filter

Default: Usually FALSE (no time restrictions)

Close All Trades at Time End

Options: TRUE/FALSE

Function: If TRUE, closes all trades when session ends

Risk: May close profitable trades prematurely

Enable Weekend Trading

Options: TRUE/FALSE

Function: Allow or block weekend trades

Note: Most forex markets closed on weekends

⏰ Time Configuration
Trading Start Hour

Format: HH:MM (24-hour format)

Example: 09:00 (session start time)

Trading End Hour

Format: HH:MM (24-hour format)

Example: 18:00 (session end time)

📅 Daily Parameters (Monday - Sunday)
📊 Individual Day Configuration:
  • Start Hour/Minute: When trading starts for that specific day
  • End Hour/Minute: When trading stops for that specific day
  • Enable/Disable: Turn trading on/off for specific days

🌍 Timezone Considerations

⚠️ Critical Timezone Note: These schedules are typically set using the broker's server timezone (often GMT+2 or GMT+3). If your broker uses a different timezone, you must adjust accordingly.
🕐 Timezone Adjustment Example:
  • Default setting: GMT+3
  • Your broker: GMT-3
  • Adjustment needed: Subtract 6 hours from default times
  • Result: If default is 09:00, set 03:00 for your broker

📊 Common Trading Hour Strategies

🌅 Asian Session Focus

Hours: 00:00 - 09:00 GMT

Pairs: JPY, AUD, NZD pairs

Characteristics: Lower volatility, range trading

🌍 European Session Focus

Hours: 08:00 - 17:00 GMT

Pairs: EUR, GBP, CHF pairs

Characteristics: High volatility, trend trading

🌎 American Session Focus

Hours: 13:00 - 22:00 GMT

Pairs: USD, CAD pairs

Characteristics: High volume, news impact

⚡ Overlap Sessions

London-NY: 13:00 - 17:00 GMT

Benefits: Highest liquidity and volatility

Risk: Increased spread and slippage

💡 Best Practices

🎯 Recommended Configurations:
  • Conservative: Trade only during major session overlaps
  • Balanced: Avoid weekends and major news hours
  • Aggressive: 24/5 trading with news filters only
⚠️ Important Warnings:
  • News Events: Consider major economic announcements
  • Market Holidays: Account for regional market closures
  • Broker Spreads: Some hours have wider spreads
  • Liquidity: Avoid very low liquidity hours

🔧 Configuration Examples

📊 Conservative Scalping Setup:
  • Monday-Thursday: 08:00 - 17:00 (European session)
  • Friday: 08:00 - 15:00 (avoid weekend gap risk)
  • Weekend Trading: FALSE
  • Close at End: TRUE (avoid overnight positions)
📊 Swing Trading Setup:
  • Monday-Friday: 01:00 - 23:00 (almost 24/5)
  • Weekend Trading: FALSE
  • Close at End: FALSE (allow position holding)
  • News Filter: Recommended in addition

🔢 Magic Numbers

🎯 Magic Number for Manual Trades

❓ What is it?

A unique number that identifies trades opened from the EA's manual panel.

🎯 Usage

Allows the EA to distinguish these trades from automatic ones, preventing them from mixing.

💡 Recommendation: Keep it different from automatic trades and any other EA you use. Example: 123456.

🤖 Magic Number for Automatic Trades

❓ What is it?

A unique number for trades opened by the EA in automatic mode.

🎯 Usage

Allows separating management of 100% automatic trades.

📊 Recommendation: Use a different value from manual and different on each chart/symbol where you load ARIA:
  • EURUSD: 789012
  • GBPUSD: 789013
  • XAUUSD: 789014
⚠️ Very Important: If you repeat magic numbers on multiple charts, one EA can close or modify trades from another pair (critical conflict).

💬 Comments

✍️ Comment for Manual Trades

❓ What is it?

The comment that MT5 will show in the Comment column for manual trades opened with ARIA's panel.

🎯 Usage

Simply to visually identify those trades in the history or terminal.

📊 Example: MANUAL

🤖 Comment for Automatic Trades

❓ What is it?

The comment that MT5 will show for trades opened automatically by AI.

🎯 Usage

Also just to easily differentiate them in the history.

📊 Example: AUTO

🎨 Chart Styler Options

📋 Chart Display Settings

These parameters control the visual appearance of your MT5 chart when using ARIA V4.

🔲 1. Show Grid on Chart

🎯 Function

Shows or hides the chart grid.

  • true: Grid is visible
  • false: Clean chart without grid

🎨 2. Chart Background Color

🎯 Function

Chart background color.

📊 Example: 52,36,12 → dark brown. You can use RGB code or choose a standard color.

📝 3. Chart Foreground Color

🎯 Function

Color of chart texts and axes (price, time, etc.).

📊 Example: SteelBlue → steel blue color.

📈 4. Bar Up Color

🎯 Function

Color of bullish bars (when close > open).

📊 Example: Green.

🟢 5. Candle Bull Color

🎯 Function

Color of bullish candles.

💡 Standard: Usually green for buy signals.

📉 6. Bar Down Color

🎯 Function

Color of bearish bars (when close < open).

📊 Example: Red.

🔴 7. Candle Bear Color

🎯 Function

Color of bearish candles.

💡 Standard: Usually red for sell signals.

📊 8. Show Volumes on Chart

🎯 Function

Shows or hides the volume indicator at the bottom of the chart.

  • true: Show volumes
  • false: Hide volumes

📈 9. Volume Color

🎯 Function

Color of the volume histogram bars.

📊 Example: White.

💡 Chart Styling Best Practices

🎯 Recommended Color Schemes:
  • Dark Theme: Dark background with light text for night trading
  • Light Theme: Light background with dark text for day trading
  • Professional: Neutral colors (grays, blues) for clear analysis
⚠️ Important Considerations:
  • Contrast: Ensure good contrast between background and text
  • Eye Strain: Choose colors that don't cause fatigue during long sessions
  • Consistency: Use consistent color scheme across all charts

📊 Technical Indicators

📊 Classic Indicators

ARIA V4 uses a combination of classic technical indicators for market analysis. Each indicator can be configured according to your trading style.

📈 1. RSI (Relative Strength Index)

⚙️ Configuration
  • Period: 14 (standard)
  • Usage: Identifies overbought (>70) and oversold (<30)
🎯 Recommendations by Style:
  • Scalping: 7–9 periods (more sensitive)
  • Intraday: 14 (balanced)
  • Swing: 21 (more stable)

📊 2. ATR (Average True Range)

⚙️ Configuration
  • Period: 14
  • Usage: Measures average volatility in pips. Used to adjust SL/TP
🎯 Recommendations by Style:
  • Scalping: ATR(7)
  • Intraday: ATR(14)
  • Swing: ATR(20)

📈 3. MA200 (Simple or Exponential Moving Average 200)

⚙️ Configuration
  • Usage: Long-term trend, institutional reference
  • Recommendation: Keep at 200, always valid for any style

📊 4. MA50

⚙️ Configuration
  • Usage: Medium-term trend, dynamic support
  • Recommendation: Keep at 50, useful to detect faster changes than MA200

📈 5. MACD (Moving Average Convergence Divergence)

⚙️ Configuration
  • Fast: 12
  • Slow: 26
  • Signal: 9
  • Usage: Momentum and trend crossovers
💡 Recommendation: Keep standard values (12,26,9). They are the most used and reliable.

📊 6. Stochastic Oscillator

⚙️ Configuration
  • K: 5
  • D: 3
  • Smooth: 3
  • Usage: Overbought/oversold and reversal signals
🎯 Recommendations by Style:
  • Scalping: 5,3,3 (more reactive)
  • Swing: 14,3,3 (less noise)

📈 7. BB (Bollinger Bands)

⚙️ Configuration
  • Period: 20
  • Deviation: 2.0 (standard)
  • Usage: Volatility and range breakouts
💡 Recommendation: Keep at 20/2.0 → classic and most effective configuration.

📊 8. Fib (Fibonacci)

⚙️ Configuration
  • Period: 20
  • Usage: Draws automatic Fibonacci retracements based on last 20 periods
🎯 Recommendation: Keep at 20. You can expand to 50 if seeking broader levels.

📈 9. S/R (Soporte/Resistencia automático)

⚙️ Configuration
  • Period: 20
  • Usage: Detection of key support and resistance levels in last 20 candles
🎯 Recommendations by Style:
  • Intraday: 20–50
  • Swing: 50–100

📊 10. Vol (Volumen)

⚙️ Configuration
  • Period: 14
  • Usage: Confirm movements by volume
💡 Recommendation: Keep at 14, sufficient to validate accumulation/distribution.

⚡ Volatility Thresholds

These numbers are normalized ATR limit levels for each timeframe.

📊 Example: M5L = 0.10 → if volatility is below 0.10, EA considers the market "flat".
🔧 Main Parameters
  • MXL/MNH (Monthly Low/High): Define monthly volatility extremes
  • Function: Advanced filters that adjust EA sensitivity to market movement
⚠️ Recommendation:
  • Don't touch unless you have experience measuring volatility
  • These are advanced filters for experienced users
  • They adjust EA sensitivity to market movement
Diagnosis

🚫 ARIA Not Opening Trades

Complete checklist to diagnose why ARIA is not executing any trades.

🔍 Systematic Diagnosis: Follow this checklist step by step to identify and solve the issue preventing ARIA from opening trades.

📋 Basic Configuration Checklist

✅ Step 1: AutoTrading Verification

✅ Step 2: WebRequest Configuration

✅ Step 3: API Key Verification

🔧 Advanced Configuration Checklist

✅ Step 4: AI Configuration

✅ Step 5: Filters and Restrictions

✅ Step 6: Market Conditions

🔍 Advanced Diagnosis

✅ Step 7: AI Response Verification

✅ Step 8: Filter Combination Check

🎯 Quick Solutions

🚀 Most Common Quick Fixes

🔧 1. Reduce Filters Temporarily
Quick Test:
  • Disable News Filter temporarily
  • Set Spread Filter to higher value
  • Reduce Minimum Confidence to 60%
  • Disable Fractal confirmations temporarily
🔧 2. Check Market Timing
Timing Issues:
  • Verify you're trading during active market hours
  • Check if it's weekend (most forex markets closed)
  • Confirm your timezone conversion is correct
  • Look for major news events blocking trades
🔧 3. Simplify Configuration
Back to Basics:
  • Use single AI instead of multiple
  • Disable all filters except spread
  • Set confidence to 65%
  • Enable debug mode to see AI responses

📊 Expected Logs When Working

✅ What You Should See in Experts Tab

🟢 Normal Operation Logs: 
✅ ARIA: AI query sent successfully
🤖 AI Response: BUY recommendation, confidence 72%
🧠 XGBoost: SL=45.2 TP=90.4 Conf=68%
📊 Trade opened: BUY 0.10 EURUSD at 1.0950
🔴 Problem Indicators: 
❌ ARIA: HTTP error 401 - Invalid API key
❌ ARIA: Spread too high (15.2 > 10.0)
❌ ARIA: News filter blocking trades
❌ ARIA: AI confidence too low (45% < 65%)

🔧 Step-by-Step Debugging Process

🎯 Systematic Approach

  1. 🔍 Check Experts Tab First
    • Press Ctrl+T to open Terminal
    • Go to "Experts" tab
    • Look for ARIA messages and errors
  2. 🤖 Verify AI Communication
    • Look for "AI query sent" messages
    • Check for HTTP errors or API failures
    • Verify AI is giving BUY/SELL recommendations
  3. 📊 Check Filter Messages
    • Look for "blocked by" messages
    • Identify which filter is preventing trades
    • Temporarily disable problematic filters
  4. ⚙️ Test with Minimal Configuration
    • Disable all filters except essential ones
    • Use single AI with 65% confidence
    • Test during active market hours
  5. 📈 Monitor for 30 Minutes
    • Let EA run with simplified settings
    • Watch Experts tab for activity
    • Gradually re-enable filters one by one

⚠️ Common Blocking Scenarios

🚫 Why ARIA Might Not Trade

🕐 Time-Related Blocks
  • Outside trading hours: EA configured for different timezone
  • Weekend trading disabled: Trying to trade on Saturday/Sunday
  • News events: Major economic announcements blocking trades
📊 Market Condition Blocks
  • High spread: Spread exceeds maximum allowed
  • Low volatility: Market too quiet for configured thresholds
  • High volatility: Market too chaotic for safe entry
🤖 AI-Related Blocks
  • Low AI confidence: All AI responses below minimum threshold
  • AI recommends WAIT: No clear directional signal
  • Multiple AI disagreement: No consensus in voting system
🔧 Technical Blocks
  • Insufficient margin: Account can't open new positions
  • Existing positions: Overtrade control preventing new entries
  • Profit/Loss limits: Daily limits already reached

💡 Emergency Reset Procedure

🔄 Last Resort: Complete Reset

⚠️ If nothing else works, try this emergency procedure:
  1. 📥 Load Default Preset
    • Use a known working preset from community
    • Don't modify any parameters initially
  2. 🔑 Re-enter API Key
    • Copy fresh API key from OpenRouter
    • Paste in EA and save preset
  3. ⏰ Wait for Active Market Hours
    • Test during London or New York session
    • Avoid low-activity periods
  4. 📊 Monitor Experts Tab
    • Watch for first AI query
    • Verify AI response and confidence
    • Look for trade execution
💡 Success Indicator: You should see AI queries and responses within 5-10 minutes during active market hours.

📞 When to Seek Support

🆘 Contact Support If:

  • ✅ All checklist items passed but still no trades
  • 🤖 AI queries working but no trade execution
  • 📊 Logs show errors you can't resolve
  • ⏰ 24+ hours without any trade activity during active markets
📋 When contacting support, provide:
  • Screenshots of your EA configuration
  • Experts tab logs from last 2 hours
  • Your broker name and timezone
  • Symbol and timeframe you're trading
Conflicts

⚠️ Incompatibilities

Critical parameter conflicts and compatibility issues you must avoid in ARIA V4.

🚨 Warning: These combinations can cause system malfunctions, unexpected behavior, or complete EA failure. Always check these incompatibilities before configuring your EA.

🚨 Critical Problems

❌ Trailing Stop + Breakeven

🔧 The Problem

Both systems want to move the Stop Loss (SL).

⚠️ Conflict Details
  • Breakeven: Wants to move SL to entry point
  • Trailing Stop: Wants to move SL continuously following price
  • Result: System doesn't work correctly - competing controls
🚫 Never Use Together: Choose either Trailing Stop OR Breakeven, never both simultaneously.

❌ Mid-Trade Queries + Trailing/Breakeven

🔧 The Problem

Mid-Trade analyzes original SL/TP levels.

⚠️ Conflict Details
  • Mid-Trade AI: Analyzes static original levels
  • Trailing/Breakeven: Changes those levels dynamically
  • Result: EA can interpret erroneous data → inconsistent decisions
🚫 Incompatible Combination: Disable Mid-Trade if using Trailing or Breakeven systems.

❌ Hidden SL/TP + Trailing/Breakeven

🔧 The Problem

Hidden SL/TP managed internally, but Trailing/Breakeven need to move them on broker.

⚠️ Conflict Details
  • Hidden SL/TP: Levels managed internally by EA
  • Trailing/Breakeven: Need to move levels on broker server
  • Result: Risk of desynchronization or closure failures
🚫 Critical Incompatibility: Use Hidden SL/TP only with static level management.

🔶 Moderate Problems

⚠️ Overly Strict Filters + Very Low AI Confidence

📊 Example Configuration
  • Minimum confidence: 50%
  • Fractals: 4 timeframes
  • News filter: Enabled
  • Result: Almost no trades executed
💡 Solution: Balance filters - if using multiple strict filters, increase AI confidence threshold or reduce filter quantity.

⚠️ Overlapping Timeframes in Fractals

🔧 The Problem

Including the trading timeframe within fractal confirmations.

📊 Example
  • Trading on: M15
  • Fractal includes: M15, H1, H4
  • Result: Double redundant confirmation and unnecessary blocks
💡 Solution: Use fractal timeframes higher than your trading timeframe.

⚠️ Additional Timeframe + Fractals Misconfigured

🔧 The Problem

Both requesting validation on the same timeframe.

⚠️ Impact
  • Overweight confirmations: Too much validation on same timeframe
  • Frequency drop: Significant reduction in trade opportunities
  • Result: Over-filtering leads to missed trades
💡 Solution: Use different timeframes for Additional TF and Fractal confirmations.

⚠️ News Filter + Spread Filter + Volatility Thresholds Together

🔧 The Problem

In high volatility markets (e.g., GOLD), it's normal for all to coincide.

📊 What Happens
  • News events: Block trading
  • High spreads: Block trading
  • High volatility: Block trading
  • Result: EA spends long periods without operating because all filters block simultaneously
💡 Solution: For volatile assets like GOLD, use maximum 2 of these 3 filters.

⚠️ Minor Compatibility Problems

🔸 Hidden SL/TP + Unstable Connection (No VPS)

🔧 The Problem

If platform crashes, there are no stops on broker.

⚠️ Risk
  • Connection loss: Hidden levels become inactive
  • No broker protection: Only safety SL remains
  • Result: Risk of unlimited losses
🚫 Not Recommended: Hidden SL/TP without VPS or very stable connection.

🔸 Support/Resistance + Very Tight ATR

🔧 The Problem

Can place stops too close to key levels.

📊 Impact
  • Premature closures: Even when direction is correct
  • Tight stops: Near support/resistance levels
  • Result: Good trades closed too early
💡 Solution: Use wider ATR settings when S/R filter is active.

🔸 Bullish Engulfing H4 + Multiple Fractals

🔧 The Problem

Both filters request trend confirmation on higher timeframes.

📊 Impact
  • Double filtering: Both look for bullish confirmation
  • Reduced opportunities: Drastically fewer BUY trades
  • Over-confirmation: Too many requirements for same direction
💡 Solution: Use either Bullish Engulfing OR Fractal confirmations for BUY trades, not both.

🔸 Volume Filter + News Filter

🔧 The Problem

During news, volume usually spikes.

⚠️ Contradiction
  • Volume filter: May allow trade due to high volume
  • News filter: Blocks trade due to news event
  • Result: Conflicting signals and missed opportunities
💡 Solution: Configure volume filter to also block during news events, or disable one of them.

💡 Additional Incompatibilities

🔸 High Frequency Parameters + Multiple AI Consultation

🔧 The Problem

Very frequent AI queries with multiple AIs increase costs and latency.

📊 Impact
  • High costs: Multiple AIs queried frequently
  • Slower responses: Multiple API calls per decision
  • API limits: Risk of hitting rate limits
💡 Solution: Use single AI for high-frequency trading, or reduce query frequency with multiple AIs.

🔸 XGBoost ML + Very Low Confidence Threshold

🔧 The Problem

XGBoost provides high-confidence predictions, but low threshold accepts weak signals.

📊 Impact
  • Contradictory logic: Advanced ML with weak signal acceptance
  • Noise trading: May execute on poor-quality signals
  • Reduced effectiveness: XGBoost advantage diminished
💡 Solution: When using XGBoost, maintain confidence threshold at 70%+ to leverage ML accuracy.

✅ Best Practices to Avoid Conflicts

🎯 Configuration Guidelines

📋 Checklist Before Going Live:
  1. Choose ONE position management system: Trailing OR Breakeven OR Static
  2. If using Hidden SL/TP: Disable Mid-Trade, Trailing, and Breakeven
  3. Limit filter combinations: Maximum 3-4 active filters simultaneously
  4. Balance AI confidence with filters: More filters = higher confidence needed
  5. Test combinations on demo: Always verify compatibility before live trading
  6. Monitor performance: Watch for unexpected behavior or lack of trades
🔧 Remember: ARIA V4 is highly configurable, but with great power comes great responsibility. Understanding these incompatibilities will help you create robust, profitable configurations.
Troubleshooting

Common Issues & Solutions

Solutions for common ARIA V4 issues.

🚫 WebRequest Issues

Solution: Ensure all URLs are added to WebRequest whitelist in MT5 settings.

🔑 API Key Problems

Solution: Verify API keys are correctly formatted and have sufficient credits.

⚠️ AutoTrading Disabled

Solution: Check AutoTrading is enabled in Options, Toolbar, and EA Properties.
